Canada">NDP</a>)</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Area<span style="font-weight:normal"><sup class="reference" (439.43\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Land</th>\n<td>1,117.11\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup> (431.32\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Water</th>\n<td>21\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup> (8\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_519" title="Area code 519">226</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_905" title="Area code 905">289</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_519" title="Area code 519">519</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" Ontario">Highways</a></th>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><img alt="" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="339" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ontario_QEW.svg/14px-Ontario_QEW.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ontario_QEW.svg/21px-Ontario_QEW.svg.png Elizabeth Way</a><br/>\n<span class="nowrap"><img alt="" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="210" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ontario_6.svg/13px-Ontario_6.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ontario_6.svg/20px-Ontario_6.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ontario_6.svg/27px-Ontario_6.svg.png 2x" width="13"/>\xc2\xa0</span><a href="/wiki/Ontario_Highway_6" title="Ontario Highway 6">Highway\xc2\xa06</a><br/>\n<span class="nowrap"><img alt="" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="210" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Ontario_20.svg/13px-Ontario_20.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Ontario_20.svg/20px-Ontario_20.svg.png 20">Highway\xc2\xa020</a><br/>\n<span class="nowrap"><img alt="" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="210" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ontario_403.svg/13px-Ontario_403.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ontario_403.svg/20px-Ontario_403.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ontario_403.svg/27px-Ontario_403.svg.png 2x" width="13"/>\xc2\xa0</span><a href="/wiki/Ontario_Highway_403" title="Ontario Highway 403">Highway\xc2\xa0403</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th scope="row">Website</th>\n<td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://www.hamilton.ca" rel="nofollow">www<wbr/>.hamilton<wbr/>.ca</a></span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hamilton</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="\'h\' in \'hi\'">h</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="/\xc9\x99l/: \'le\' in \'bottle\'">\xc9\x99l</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\xc9\x99n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Canada_2016_Census" title="Canada 2016 Census">2016 population</a> 536,917; <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">UA</a> population 683,645; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_Metropolitan_Area" title="Census Metropolitan Area">CMA</a> population 778,400)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[a]</a></sup> is a port city in the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>. Conceived by <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(politician)" title="George Hamilton (politician)">George Hamilton</a> when he purchased the <a href="/wiki/James_Durand" title="James Durand">Durand</a> farm shortly after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WEAVER1985_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-WEAVER1985-11">[10]</a></sup> Hamilton has become the centre of a densely populated and industrialized region at the west end of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a>. On January 1, 2001, the new City of Hamilton was formed through the amalgamation of the former city and the other constituent lower-tier municipalities of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_Municipality_of_Hamilton-Wentworth,_Ontario" title="Regional Municipality of Hamilton-Wentworth, Ontario">Regional Municipality of Hamilton-Wentworth</a> with the upper-tier regional government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amalgprovles_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-amalgprovles-12">[11]</a></sup> Residents of the old city are known as Hamiltonians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HAM100_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-HAM100-13">[12]</a></sup> Since 1981, the metropolitan area has been listed as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_100_largest_metropolitan_areas_in_Canada" title="List of the 100 largest metropolitan areas in Canada">ninth largest in Canada</a> and the third largest in Ontario.</p>\n<p>Hamilton is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens,_Ontario" title="Royal Botanical Gardens, Ontario">Royal Botanical Gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Warplane_Heritage_Museum" title="Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum">Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Trail" title="Bruce Trail">Bruce Trail</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redeemer_University_College" title="Redeemer University College">Redeemer University College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_College" title="Mohawk College">Mohawk College</a>. McMaster University is ranked 4th in Canada and 94th in the world by Times Higher Education Rankings 2015-16 and has a well-known <a href="/wiki/Michael_G._DeGroote_School_of_Medicine" title="Michael G. DeGroote School of Medicine">medical school</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Tiger-Cats" title="Hamilton Tiger-Cats">Hamilton Tiger-Cats</a> began playing at the new <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons_Field" title="Tim Hortons Field">Tim Hortons Field</a> in 2014, which was built as part of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Pan_American_Games" title="2015 Pan American Games">2015 Pan American Games</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Football Hall of Fame">Canadian Football Hall of Fame</a> can also be found.</p>\n<p>Possibly because of its diverse environment, numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_films_shot_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of films shot in Hamilton, Ontario">TV and film productions</a> have been filmed in Hamilton, regulated by the Hamilton Film and Television Office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamfilm_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamfilm-15">[14]</a></sup> A growing arts and culture community garnered media attention in 2006 when the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globe_and_Mail" title="Globe and Mail">Globe and Mail</a></i> published an article called "Go West, Young Artist" about Hamilton\'s growing art scene. The article highlighted local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_galleries" title="Art galleries">art galleries</a>, recording studios and independent film production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOWEST_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-GOWEST-16">[15]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Crime"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Crime</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Attractions"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Attractions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Sister_cities"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sister cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="History of Hamilton, Ontario">History of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/220px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/330px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/440px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalists" title="United Empire Loyalists">United Empire Loyalists</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In pre-<a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">colonial</a> times, the <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Nation" title="Neutral Nation">Neutral Indians</a> used much of the land but were gradually driven out by the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Five (later Six) Nations</a> (Iroquois) who were allied with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_under_British_Imperial_control_(1764-1867)" title="Canada under British Imperial control (1764-1867)">British</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">Huron</a> and their French allies. A member of the Iroquois Confederacy provided the route and name for <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_Road_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="Mohawk Road (Hamilton, Ontario)">Mohawk Road</a>, which originally included King Street in the lower city.</p>\n<p>Following the United States gaining independence after their American Revolutionary War, in 1784, about 10,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalists" title="United Empire Loyalists">United Empire Loyalists</a> settled in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> (what is now southern Ontario), chiefly in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_Municipality_of_Niagara,_Ontario" title="Regional Municipality of Niagara, Ontario">Niagara</a>, around the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Quinte" title="Bay of Quinte">Bay of Quinte</a>, and along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> between <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. The Crown granted them land in these areas in order to develop Upper Canada and to compensate them for losses in the United States. With former First Nations lands available for purchase, these new settlers were soon followed by many more Americans, attracted by the availability of inexpensive, arable land. At the same time, large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a> who had been allied with Britain arrived from the United States and were settled on reserves west of Lake Ontario as compensation for lands they lost in what was now the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOYALISTS_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-LOYALISTS-17">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The town of Hamilton was conceived by <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(politician)" title="George Hamilton (politician)">George Hamilton</a> (a son of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queenston" title="Queenston">Queenston</a> entrepreneur and founder, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Hamilton_(1753-1809)" title="Robert Hamilton (1753-1809)">Robert Hamilton</a>), when he purchased farm holdings of <a href="/wiki/James_Durand" title="James Durand">James Durand</a>, the local Member of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Upper_Canada" title="Legislative Assembly of Upper Canada">British Legislative Assembly</a>, shortly after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WEAVER1985_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-WEAVER1985-11">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Hughson" title="Nathaniel Hughson">Nathaniel Hughson</a>, a property owner to the north, cooperated with George Hamilton to prepare a proposal for a courthouse and jail on Hamilton\'s property. Hamilton offered the land to the crown for the future site. Durand was empowered by Hughson and Hamilton to sell property holdings which later became the site of the town. As he had been instructed, Durand circulated the offers at <a href="/wiki/York,_Upper_Canada" title="York, Upper Canada">York</a> during a session of the Legislative Assembly, which established a new <a href="/wiki/Gore_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Gore District, Upper Canada">Gore District</a>, of which the Hamilton townsite was a member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WEAVER1985_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-WEAVER1985-11">[10]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Initially, this town was not the most important centre of the Gore District. An early indication of Hamilton\xe2\x80\x99s sudden prosperity was signaled by the fact that in 1816 it was chosen over <a href="/wiki/Ancaster,_Ontario" title="Ancaster, Ontario">Ancaster, Ontario</a> that year to be the administrative center for the new Gore District. Another dramatic economic turnabout for Hamilton occurred in 1832 when a canal was finally cut through the outer sand bar that enabled Hamilton to become a major port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> A permanent jail was not constructed until 1832, when a cut-stone design was completed on Prince\'s Square, one of the two squares created in 1816.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WEAVER1985_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-WEAVER1985-11">[10]</a></sup> Subsequently, the first police board and the town limits were defined by statute on February 13, 1833.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Official city status was achieved on June 9, 1846, by an act of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a>, 9 Victoria Chapter 73.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1846est_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-1846est-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>By 1845, the population was 6,475. In 1846, there were useful roads to many communities as well as stage coaches and steamboats to Toronto, Queenston, and Niagara. Eleven cargo schooners were owned in Hamilton. Eleven churches were in operation. A reading room provided access to newspapers from other cities and from England and the U.S. In addition to stores of all types, four banks, tradesmen of various types, and sixty-five taverns, industry in the community included three breweries, ten importers of dry goods and groceries, five importers of hardware, two tanneries, three coachmakers, and a marble and a stone works. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As the city grew, several prominent buildings were constructed in the late 19th century, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Lodge_of_Canada" title="Grand Lodge of Canada">Grand Lodge of Canada</a> in 1855,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRANDLODGE_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-GRANDLODGE-21">[20]</a></sup> West Flamboro Methodist Church in 1879 (later purchased by Dufferin Masonic Lodge in 1893),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dufferin_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-dufferin-22">[21]</a></sup> a public library in 1890, and the Right House department store in 1893. The first commercial telephone service in Canada, the first telephone exchange in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, and the second telephone exchange in all of North America were each established in the city between 1877\xe2\x80\x9378.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-headlake_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-headlake-23">[22]</a></sup> The city had several interurban electric street railways and two inclines, all powered by the Cataract Power Co.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG/220px-ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG/330px-ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG/440px-ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ScottishRiteCastleHamilton.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nScottish Rite Castle</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Though suffering through the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Street_Railway" title="Hamilton Street Railway">Hamilton Street Railway</a> strike of 1906, with industrial businesses expanding, Hamilton\'s population doubled between 1900 and 1914. Two steel manufacturing companies, <a href="/wiki/Stelco" title="Stelco">Stelco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dofasco" title="Dofasco">Dofasco</a>, were formed in 1910 and 1912, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Beech-Nut" title="Beech-Nut">Beech-Nut Packing Company</a> opened manufacturing plants in 1914 and 1922, respectively, their first outside the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HISINDI_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-HISINDI-25">[24]</a></sup> Population and economic growth continued until the 1960s. In 1929 the city\'s first high-rise building, the Pigott Building, was constructed; that year <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a> moved from Toronto to Hamilton, in 1934 the second <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Tire" title="Canadian Tire">Canadian Tire</a> store in Canada opened here; in 1940 the airport was completed; and in 1948, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studebaker_Canada_Ltd." title="Studebaker Canada Ltd.">Studebaker</a> assembly line was constructed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj45_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-memproj45-26">[25]</a></sup> Infrastructure and retail development continued, with the [[Burlington Bay James N. Allan Skyway opening in 1958, and the first <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons" title="Tim Hortons">Tim Hortons</a> store in 1964.</p>\n<p>Since then, many of the large industries have moved or shut down operations in restructuring that also affected the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HISINDI_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-HISINDI-25">[24]</a></sup> The economy has shifted more toward the service sector, such as transportation, education, and health services.</p>\n<p>On January 1, 2001, the new city of Hamilton was formed from the amalgamation of Hamilton and its five neighbouring municipalities: <a href="/wiki/Ancaster,_Ontario" title="Ancaster, Ontario">Ancaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dundas,_Ontario" title="Dundas, Ontario">Dundas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flamborough,_Ontario" title="Flamborough, Ontario">Flamborough</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glanbrook,_Ontario" title="Glanbrook, Ontario">Glanbrook</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stoney_Creek,_Ontario" title="Stoney Creek, Ontario">Stoney Creek</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amalgprovles_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-amalgprovles-12">[11]</a></sup> Before amalgamation, the "old" City of Hamilton had 331,121 Hamiltonians divided into 100 neighbourhoods. The former region of Hamilton-Wentworth had a population of 490,268. The amalgamation created a single-tier municipal government ending subsidization of its suburbs. The new amalgamated city has 519,949 people in more than 100 neighbourhoods, and surrounding communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTSTEPS_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTSTEPS-27">[26]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1997 there was a devastating fire at the Plastimet plastics plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Approximately 300 firefighters battled the blaze, and many sustained severe chemical burns and inhaled <a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">volatile organic compounds</a> when at least 400 tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">PVC</a> plastic were consumed in the fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Geography of Hamilton, Ontario">Geography of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Transportation in Hamilton, Ontario">Transportation in Hamilton, Ontario</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_streets_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of streets in Hamilton, Ontario">List of streets in Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<p>Hamilton is located in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a> on the western end of the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Peninsula" title="Niagara Peninsula">Niagara Peninsula</a> and wraps around the westernmost part of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>; most of the city, including the downtown section, is on the south shore. Hamilton is situated in the geographic centre of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a> and is roughly the midway point between <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a>, although slightly closer to the former. Its major physical features are Hamilton Harbour, marking the northern limit of the city, and the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Escarpment" title="Niagara Escarpment">Niagara Escarpment</a> running through the middle of the city across its entire breadth, bisecting the city into "upper" and "lower" parts. The maximum high point is 250m (820\') above the level of Lake Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-30">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to all records from local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historians" title="Historians">historians</a>, this district was called <i>Attiwandaronia</i> by the native <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Nation" title="Neutral Nation">Neutral people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAGA_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAGA-31">[30]</a></sup> The first aboriginals to settle in the Hamilton area called the bay <i>Macassa</i>, meaning "beautiful waters".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTSTEPS_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTSTEPS-27">[26]</a></sup> Hamilton is one of 11 cities showcased in the book, <i>Green City: People, Nature &amp; Urban Places</i> by Quebec author Mary Soderstrom, which examines the city as an example of an industrial powerhouse co-existing with nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GREENCITY_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-GREENCITY-32">[31]</a></sup> Soderstrom credits <a href="/wiki/Thomas_McQuesten" title="Thomas McQuesten">Thomas McQuesten</a> and family in the 1930s who "became champions of parks, greenspace and roads" in Hamilton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GREENCITY2_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-GREENCITY2-33">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour" title="Hamilton Harbour">Hamilton Harbour</a> is a natural harbour with a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandbar" title="Sandbar">sandbar</a> called the Beachstrip. This sandbar was deposited during a period of higher lake levels during the last <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">ice age</a>, and extends southeast through the central lower city to the escarpment. Hamilton\'s deep sea port is accessed by ship canal through the beach strip into the harbour and is traversed by two bridges, the QEW\'s <a href="/wiki/Burlington_Bay_James_N._Allan_Skyway" title="Burlington Bay James N. Allan Skyway">Burlington Bay James N. Allan Skyway</a> and the lower Canal Lift Bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bay-34">[33]</a></sup><br/></p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="">\n<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Project2.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Hamilton Harbour from T.B. McQuesten High Level Bridge on York Boulevard, near Harvey Park."><img alt="" data-file-height="987" data-file-width="8962" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Hamilton_Project2.jpg/900px-Hamilton_Project2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Hamilton_Project2.jpg/1350px-Hamilton_Project2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Hamilton_Project2.jpg/1800px-Hamilton_Project2.jpg 2x" width="900"/></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Project2.jpg" title="File:Hamilton Project2.jpg"></a></div>\nPanoramic view of Hamilton Harbour from T.B. McQuesten High Level Bridge on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/York_Boulevard_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="York Boulevard (Hamilton, Ontario)">York Boulevard</a>, near Harvey Park.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Between 1788 and 1793, the townships at the Head-of-the-Lake were surveyed and named. The area was first known as The Head-of-the-Lake for its location at the western end of Lake Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-headlake_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-headlake-23">[22]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=John_Ryckman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="John Ryckman (page does not exist)">John Ryckman</a>, born in Barton township (where present day downtown Hamilton is), described the area in 1803 as he remembered it: "The city in 1803 was all forest. The shores of the bay were difficult to reach or see because they were hidden by a thick, almost impenetrable mass of trees and undergrowth\xc2\xa0... Bears ate pigs, so settlers warred on bears. Wolves gobbled sheep and geese, so they hunted and trapped wolves. They also held organized raids on rattlesnakes on the mountainside. There was plenty of game. Many a time have I seen (sic) a deer jump the fence into my back yard, and there were millions of pigeons which we clubbed as they flew low."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barton2_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-barton2-35">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1488" data-file-width="1984" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg/220px-Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg/330px-Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg/440px-Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waterdawn_Webster_Falls5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Webster%27s_Falls" title="Webster\'s Falls">Webster\'s Falls</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spencer_Gorge_/_Webster%27s_Falls_Conservation_Area" title="Spencer Gorge / Webster\'s Falls Conservation Area">Spencer Gorge / Webster\'s Falls Conservation Area</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:495px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3134" data-file-width="7964" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hamilton4.jpg/493px-Hamilton4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hamilton4.jpg/740px-Hamilton4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hamilton4.jpg/986px-Hamilton4.jpg 2x" width="493"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Albion_Falls" title="Albion Falls">Albion Falls</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(politician)" title="George Hamilton (politician)">George Hamilton</a>, a settler and local politician, established a town site in the northern portion of Barton Township in 1815. He kept several east\xe2\x80\x93west roads which were originally Indian trails, but the north\xe2\x80\x93south streets were on a regular grid pattern. Streets were designated "East" or "West" if they crossed <a href="/wiki/James_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="James Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">James Street</a> or Highway 6. Streets were designated "North" or "South" if they crossed <a href="/wiki/King_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="King Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">King Street</a> or Highway 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HAMBIO1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-HAMBIO1-36">[35]</a></sup> The overall design of the townsite, likely conceived in 1816, was commonplace. George Hamilton employed a grid street pattern used in most towns in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> and throughout the American frontier. The eighty original lots had frontages of fifty feet; each lot faced a broad street and backed onto a twelve-foot lane. It took at least a decade for all of the original lots to be sold, but the construction of the Burlington Canal in 1823, and a new court-house in 1827 encouraged Hamilton to add more blocks around 1828\xe2\x80\x939. At this time, he included a market square in an effort to draw commercial activity onto his lands, but the natural growth of the town was to the north of Hamilton\'s plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamilton2_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton2-37">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Conservation_Authority" title="Hamilton Conservation Authority">Hamilton Conservation Authority</a> owns, leases or manages about 4,500 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> (11,100 <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acres</a>) of land with the city operating 1,077 hectares (2,661 acres) of parkland at 310 locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Many of the parks are located along the Niagara Escarpment, which runs from <a href="/wiki/Tobermory,_Ontario" title="Tobermory, Ontario">Tobermory</a> at the tip of the <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Peninsula" title="Bruce Peninsula">Bruce Peninsula</a> in the north, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queenston" title="Queenston">Queenston</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">Niagara River</a> in the south, and provides views of the cities and towns at the western end of Lake Ontario. The hiking path <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Trail" title="Bruce Trail">Bruce Trail</a> runs the length of the escarpment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRUCETRAIL_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRUCETRAIL-40">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_waterfalls_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of waterfalls in Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton is home to more than 100 waterfalls</a> and cascades, most of which are on or near the Bruce Trail as it winds through the Niagara Escarpment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:2008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="">\n<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg" title="Panoramic view of lower Hamilton from Sam Lawrence Park near Concession Street on the Niagara Escarpment (Hamilton Mountain)."><img alt="" data-file-height="1692" data-file-width="16131" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg/2000px-Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg/3000px-Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg/4000px-Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg 2x" width="2000"/></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_Panoramic.jpg" title="File:Hamilton Panoramic.jpg"></a></div>\nPanoramic view of lower Hamilton from Sam Lawrence Park near <a href="/wiki/Concession_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="Concession Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">Concession Street</a> on the Niagara Escarpment (Hamilton Mountain).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Hamilton\'s climate is humid-continental, characterized by changeable weather patterns. However, its climate is moderate compared with most of Canada. Hamilton\'s location on an embayment at the southwestern corner of Lake Ontario with an escarpment dividing upper and lower parts of the city results in noticeable disparities in weather over short distances. This is also the case with pollution levels, which depending on localized winds patterns or low clouds can be high in certain areas mostly originating from the city\'s steel industry mixed with regional vehicle pollution. With a July average of exactly 22.0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (71.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBGstats_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-RBGstats-42">[41]</a></sup> the lower city is located in a pocket of the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate#Dfa.2FDwa.2FDsa:_Hot_.28or_very_warm.29_summer_subtype" title="Humid continental climate"><i>Dfa</i> climate zone</a> found at the southwestern end of Lake Ontario (between Hamilton and Toronto and eastward into the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Peninsula" title="Niagara Peninsula">Niagara Peninsula</a>), while the upper reaches of the city fall into the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate#Dfb.2FDwb:_Warm_summer_subtype" title="Humid continental climate"><i>Dfb</i> climate zone</a>.</p>\n<p>The airport\'s open, rural location and higher altitude (240m vs. 85m ASL downtown) results in lower temperatures, generally windier conditions, and higher snowfall amounts than lower, built-up areas of the city. One exception is on early spring afternoons; when colder than air lake temperatures keep shoreline areas significantly cooler, under the presence of an east or north-east onshore flow.</p>\n<p>The highest temperature ever recorded in Hamilton was 41.1\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (106\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) on 14 July 1868.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamilton_.28July_1868.29_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton_.28July_1868.29-43">[42]</a></sup> The coldest temperature ever recorded was -30.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (-23\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) on 25 January 1884.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamilton_.28January_1884.29_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton_.28January_1884.29-44">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<p><br/></p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:90%; href="#cite_note-Hamilton_1866-1958-46">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamilton_RBG_CS_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton_RBG_CS-47">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-February_2017_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-February_2017-48">[46]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><br/></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population-coh-1816-2006.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="507" data-file-width="693" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Population-coh-1816-2006.png/220px-Population-coh-1816-2006.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Population-coh-1816-2006.png/330px-Population-coh-1816-2006.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Population-coh-1816-2006.png/440px-Population-coh-1816-2006.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population-coh-1816-2006.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nCity population (1816\xe2\x80\x932006)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HAMBIO1_page_143_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-HAMBIO1_page_143-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj38_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-memproj38-50">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bartont_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-bartont-51">[49]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Canada_2006_Census" title="Canada 2006 Census">2006 Canadian Census</a>, more than 20 percent of the local population was <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">not born in Canada</a>. This is the third highest such proportion in Canada after <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> at 49%, and <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> at 39%. Between 2001 and 2006, the foreign-born population increased by 7.7% while the total population of the Hamilton census metropolitan area (CMA) grew by 4.3%. The share of Canada\'s recent immigrants who settle in Hamilton has remained unchanged since 2001 at 1.9%. Hamilton was home to 20,800 immigrants who arrived in Canada between 2001 and 2006, half of whom were born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadians_of_Asian_ancestry" title="Canadians of Asian ancestry">Asia</a> and the Middle East, while nearly one-quarter (23%) were from Europe. Hamilton also had a high proportion of people with <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Canadian" title="English Canadian">English</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Canadian" title="Scottish Canadian">Scottish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Canadian" title="German Canadian">German</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Canadian" title="Irish Canadian">Irish</a> ancestry. Nearly three in ten residents reported English as their sole ethnic origin or as one of their ancestral origins. As well, nearly one in five reported Scottish ancestry either alone or in combination with another ethnic origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StatsCan07_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-StatsCan07-52">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canada_2011_Census" title="Canada 2011 Census">Canada 2011 Census</a> short form did not include questions on ethnic background or national origin. However, the 2011 National Household Survey (NHS) (a voluntary survey that accompanied the census) produced the following data:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>of 509,635 respondents, 125,010 (or 24.5 percent) were immigrants</li>\n<li>27,750 respondents (5.4 percent of total respondents) immigrated between 2001 and 2011</li>\n<li>the highest numbers of immigrants (in total) came from the following countries:\n<ol>\n<li>Italy: 11,610 (9.3 percent of immigrants)</li>\n<li>Poland: 5,950 (4.8 percent)</li>\n<li>India: 5,930 (4.7 percent)</li>\n<li>Portugal: 5,775 (4.6 percent)</li>\n<li>Philippines: 5,285 (4.2 percent)</li>\n<li>Croatia: 4,840 (3.9 percent)</li>\n<li>United States: 4,290 (3.4 percent)</li>\n<li>Iraq: 3,855 (3.1 percent)</li>\n<li>China (excluding Hong Kong and Macau): 3,740 (3.0 percent)</li>\n<li>Germany: 3,345 (2.7 percent)</li>\n</ol>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In February 2014, the city\'s council voted to declare Hamilton a <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_city" title="Sanctuary city">sanctuary city</a>, offering municipal services to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undocumented_immigrants" title="Undocumented immigrants">undocumented immigrants</a> at risk of <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hamilton also has a large French community for which provincial services are offered in French. In Ontario, urban centres where there are at least 5000 Francophones or where at least 10% of the population is francophone are designated areas where bilingual provincial services have to be offered. According to the latest statistics, the Francophone community grew by 50% between 2006 and 2011 in Hamilton, and in the city, 45,000 citizens claim to have knowledge of both official languages, amongst which 13,000 have French as a mother tongue. The Franco-Ontarian community of Hamilton boasts two school boards (Conseil scolaire Viamonde and Conseil scolaire catholique Mon-Avenir) five schools (2 secondary and 3 elementary), a community health centre that is part of the LHIN (Centre de sant\xc3\xa9 communautaire Hamilton/Niagara), a cultural centre (Centre fran\xc3\xa7ais Hamilton), three daycare centres, a provincially funded employment centre (Options Emploi), a community college site (Coll\xc3\xa8ge Bor\xc3\xa9al) and a community organization that supports the development of the francophone community in Hamilton (ACFO R\xc3\xa9gionale Hamilton).</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:281px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hamilton7.jpg/279px-Hamilton7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hamilton7.jpg/419px-Hamilton7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hamilton7.jpg/558px-Hamilton7.jpg 2x" width="279"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDowntown Hamilton view from Sam Lawrence Park</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The top countries of birth for the newcomers living in Hamilton in the 1990s were: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SFRY" title="SFRY">former Yugoslavia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_Canadian" title="Polish Canadian">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo-Canadians" title="Indo-Canadians">India</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Canadian" title="Chinese Canadian">China</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_Canadian" title="Filipino Canadian">Philippines</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Canadian" title="Iraqi Canadian">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StatsCan02_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-StatsCan02-56">[54]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Children aged 14 years and under accounted for 17.8% of the population while those 65 years of age and older constituted 14.9%, resulting in an average age of 39.6 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statscan-ham_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-statscan-ham-57">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The most described <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Canada" title="Religion in Canada">religion</a> in Hamilton is Christianity although other religions brought by immigrants are also growing. The 2011 census indicates that 67.6% of the population adheres to a Christian denomination, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholics</a> being the largest at 34.3% of the city\'s population. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christ_the_King_Cathedral_(Hamilton)" title="Christ the King Cathedral (Hamilton)">Christ the King Cathedral</a> is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Hamilton, Ontario">Diocese of Hamilton</a>. Other denominations include the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church</a> (6.5%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> (6.4%), <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a> (3.1%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">Christian Orthodox</a> (2.9%), and other denominations (9.8%). Other religions with significant populations include <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Canada" title="Islam in Canada">Islam</a> (3.7%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> (0.9%), <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikh</a> (0.8%), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> (0.8%), and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> (0.7%). Those with no religious affiliation accounted for 24.9% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Environics Analytics, a geodemographic marketing firm that created 66 different "clusters" of people complete with profiles of how they live, what they think and what they consume, sees a future Hamilton with younger upscale Hamiltonians\xe2\x80\x94who are tech savvy and university educated\xe2\x80\x94choosing to live in the downtown and surrounding areas rather than just visiting intermittently. More two and three-storey townhouses and apartments will be built on downtown lots; small condos will be built on vacant spaces in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Dundas,_Ontario" title="Dundas, Ontario">Dundas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ainslie_Wood,_Ontario" title="Ainslie Wood, Ontario">Ainslie Wood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westdale,_Ontario" title="Westdale, Ontario">Westdale</a> to accommodate newly retired seniors; and more retail and commercial zones will be created. The city is also expected to grow by more than 28,000 people and 18,000 households by the year 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FUTURE_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FUTURE-59">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The following data are recorded by the 2011 NHS survey:</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="5" cellspacing="0">\n<tr>\n<td valign="top">\n<table>\n<caption>Reported ethnic origins, 2011</caption>\n<tr style="background:#efefef;">\n<th>Ethnic origin</th>\n<th>Number of respondents<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[note 2]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>English</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">134,925</td>\n<td
