style="text-align:right;">3.5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Portuguese</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">14,610</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.9</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>North American Indian</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">13,720</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.7</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</center>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Total number of respondents was 509,635.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note that a person may report more than one ethnic origin.</span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Economy of Hamilton, Ontario">Economy of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Film_industry_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Film industry in Hamilton, Ontario">Film industry in Hamilton, Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_head_offices_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of head offices in Hamilton, Ontario">List of head offices in Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG/220px-JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG/330px-JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG/440px-JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JacksonSquareHamilton.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Lloyd_D._Jackson_Square" title="Lloyd D. Jackson Square">Lloyd D. Jackson Square</a> (Mall), Commerce Place Complex</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The most important economic activity in Ontario is manufacturing, and the Toronto\xe2\x80\x93Hamilton region is the most highly industrialized section of the country. The area from <a href="/wiki/Oshawa" title="Oshawa">Oshawa</a>, Ontario around the west end of Lake Ontario to Niagara Falls, with Hamilton at its centre, is known as the Golden Horseshoe and had a population of approximately 8.1 million people in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006CensGGH_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-2006CensGGH-63">[59]</a></sup> The phrase was first used by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Electric_(1886)" title="Westinghouse Electric (1886)">Westinghouse</a> President Herbert H. Rogge in a speech to the Hamilton Chamber of Commerce, on January 12, 1954. "Hamilton in 50 years will be the forward cleat in a golden horseshoe of industrial development from Oshawa to the Niagara River\xc2\xa0... 150 miles long and 50 miles (80\xc2\xa0km) wide...It will run from Niagara Falls on the south to about Oshawa on the north and take in numerous cities and towns already there, including Hamilton and Toronto."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bank_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bank-64">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>With sixty percent of Canada\'s steel being produced in Hamilton by <a href="/wiki/Stelco" title="Stelco">Stelco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dofasco" title="Dofasco">Dofasco</a>, the city has become known as the Steel Capital of Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelcap_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-steelcap-65">[61]</a></sup> After nearly declaring bankruptcy, Stelco returned to profitability in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelprofit_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-steelprofit-66">[62]</a></sup> On August 26, 2007 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Steel_Corporation" title="United States Steel Corporation">United States Steel Corporation</a> acquired Stelco for C$38.50 in cash per share, owning more than 76 percent of Stelco\'s outstanding shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USSTEEL_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-USSTEEL-67">[63]</a></sup> On September 17, 2014, US Steel Canada announced that it was applying for bankruptcy protection and that it would be closing down its Hamilton operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe.26Mail_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Globe.26Mail-68">[64]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton,_Ontario.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg/220px-Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg/330px-Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg/440px-Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton%2C_Ontario.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Construction_and_restoration_of_the_new_%22Bella_Towers%22_on_150_Main_Street_West_in_downtown_Hamilton,_Ontario.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nConstruction of the new "Bella Towers" on 150 Main Street West. A part of the string of new private development and investment currently happening in the downtown core.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Dofasco, in 1999, was the most profitable steel producer in North America and in 2000, the most profitable in Canada. It currently has approximately 7,300 employees at its Hamilton plant and produces over four million <a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">tons</a> of steel annually, representing about 30% of Canada\'s flat-rolled sheet steel shipments. Dofasco is one of North America\'s most profitable steel companies, and Dofasco was named to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dow_Jones" title="Dow Jones">Dow Jones</a> Sustainability World Index in 2006 for the seventh year in a row. Dofasco produces steel products for the automotive, construction, energy, manufacturing, pipe and tube, appliance, packaging, and steel distribution industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dofasco_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-dofasco-69">[65]</a></sup> Dofasco is currently a stand-alone subsidiary of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arcelor_Mittal" title="Arcelor Mittal">Arcelor Mittal</a>, the world\'s largest steel producer. Previously ordered by the U.S. Department of Justice to divest itself of the Canadian company, Arcelor Mittal has now been allowed to retain Dofasco provided it sells several of its American assets instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Originally, in the 1940s, the <a href="/wiki/John_C._Munro_Hamilton_International_Airport" title="John C. Munro Hamilton International Airport">John C. Munro Hamilton International Airport</a> was used as a wartime air force training station. Today TradePort International Corporation manages and operates the John C. Munro Hamilton International Airport. Under TradePort management, passenger traffic at the Hamilton terminal has increased from 90,000 in 1996 to approximately 900,000 in 2002. The airport\'s mid-term target for growth in its passenger service is five million air travelers annually. The air cargo sector of the airport has 24\xe2\x80\x937 operational capability and strategic geographic location, allowing its capacity to increase by 50% since 1996; 91,000\xc2\xa0<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_tonnes" title="Metric tonnes">metric tonnes</a> (100,000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">tons</a>) of cargo passed through the airport in 2002. Courier companies with operations at the airport include <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">United Parcel Service</a> and Cargojet Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airport2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-airport2-71">[67]</a></sup> In 2003, the city began developing a 30-year growth management strategy which called, in part, for a massive <a href="/wiki/Aerotropolis" title="Aerotropolis">aerotropolis</a> industrial park centred on Hamilton Airport. The aerotropolis proposal, now known as the <i>Airport Employment Growth District</i>, is touted as a solution to the city\'s shortage of employment lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirportB_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-AirportB-72">[68]</a></sup> Hamilton turned over operation of the airport to TradePort International Corp. in 1996. In 2007, YVR Airport Services (YVRAS), which runs the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_International_Airport" title="Vancouver International Airport">Vancouver International Airport</a>, took over 100 percent ownership of TradePort in a $13-million deal. The airport is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Warplane_Heritage_Museum" title="Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum">Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum</a>.</p>\n<p>A report by Hemson Consulting identified an opportunity to develop 1,000 hectares (2,500 acres) of greenfields (the size of the Royal Botanical Gardens) that could generate an estimated 90,000 jobs by 2031. A proposed <a href="/wiki/Aerotropolis" title="Aerotropolis">aerotropolis</a> industrial park at Highway 6 and 403, has been debated at City Hall for years. Opponents feel the city needs to do more investigation about the cost to taxpayers before embarking on the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Airport2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Airport2-73">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>When ranked on a "total crime severity index", Hamilton was 21st in Canada in 2011 for a metropolitan area. This was an eight percent decrease from 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> Of note was Hamilton\'s second place rank for police-reported hate crimes in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Politics of Hamilton, Ontario">Politics of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario_City_Council" title="Hamilton, Ontario City Council">Hamilton, Ontario City Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Mayors_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Category:Mayors of Hamilton, Ontario">Category:Mayors of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario_municipal_election,_2014" title="Hamilton, Ontario municipal election, 2014">Hamilton, Ontario municipal election, 2014</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG/220px-Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG/330px-Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG/440px-Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Building_Hamilton.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_Street_(Hamilton)" title="Bay Street (Hamilton)">Bay Street</a> Federal Building</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Citizens of Hamilton are represented at all three levels of Canadian government. Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/42nd_Canadian_federal_election" title="42nd Canadian federal election">2015 Federal Election</a>, representation in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada" title="Parliament of Canada">Parliament of Canada</a> will consist of five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Members_of_Parliament_(Canada)" title="Members of Parliament (Canada)">Members of Parliament</a> representing the federal ridings of <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_West%E2%80%94Ancaster%E2%80%94Dundas" title="Hamilton West\xe2\x80\x94Ancaster\xe2\x80\x94Dundas">Hamilton West\xe2\x80\x94Ancaster\xe2\x80\x94Dundas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Centre" title="Hamilton Centre">Hamilton Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_East%E2%80%94Stoney_Creek" title="Hamilton East\xe2\x80\x94Stoney Creek">Hamilton East\xe2\x80\x94Stoney Creek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Mountain" title="Hamilton Mountain">Hamilton Mountain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flamborough%E2%80%94Glanbrook" title="Flamborough\xe2\x80\x94Glanbrook">Flamborough\xe2\x80\x94Glanbrook</a>. This election will mark the first occasion in which Hamilton will have five Members of Parliament representing areas wholly within Hamilton\'s city boundaries, with previous boundaries situating rural ridings across municipal lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Provincially, there are five elected <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Provincial_Parliament_(Ontario)" title="Member of Provincial Parliament (Ontario)">Members of Provincial Parliament</a> who serve in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Ontario" title="Legislature of Ontario">Legislature of Ontario</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Municipal_Affairs_and_Housing_(Ontario)" title="Ministry of Municipal Affairs and Housing (Ontario)">Minister of Housing and Municipal Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_McMeekin" title="Ted McMeekin">Ted McMeekin</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Ontario" title="Liberal Party of Ontario">Liberal</a>), represents <a href="/wiki/Ancaster%E2%80%94Dundas%E2%80%94Flamborough%E2%80%94Westdale_(provincial_electoral_district)" title="Ancaster\xe2\x80\x94Dundas\xe2\x80\x94Flamborough\xe2\x80\x94Westdale (provincial electoral district)">Ancaster\xe2\x80\x94Dundas\xe2\x80\x94Flamborough\xe2\x80\x94Westdale</a>. Leader of the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_New_Democratic_Party" title="Ontario New Democratic Party">Ontario New Democratic Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Horwath" title="Andrea Horwath">Andrea Horwath</a>, represents <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Centre" title="Hamilton Centre">Hamilton Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Miller_(Canadian_politician)" title="Paul Miller (Canadian politician)">Paul Miller</a> (NDP) represents <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_East%E2%80%94Stoney_Creek" title="Hamilton East\xe2\x80\x94Stoney Creek">Hamilton East\xe2\x80\x94Stoney Creek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monique_Taylor" title="Monique Taylor">Monique Taylor</a> (NDP) represents <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Mountain" title="Hamilton Mountain">Hamilton Mountain</a>. Former leader of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Ontario" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Ontario">Progressive Conservative Party of Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hudak" title="Tim Hudak">Tim Hudak</a>, serves as MPP for <a href="/wiki/Niagara_West%E2%80%94Glanbrook_(provincial_electoral_district)" title="Niagara West\xe2\x80\x94Glanbrook (provincial electoral district)">Niagara West\xe2\x80\x94Glanbrook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hamilton\'s municipal government consists of one mayor, elected city wide, and 15 city councillors, elected individually by each of the city\'s wards, to serve on the Hamilton City Council. Presently, Hamilton\'s mayor is <a href="/wiki/Fred_Eisenberger" title="Fred Eisenberger">Fred Eisenberger</a>, elected on October 27, 2014 to a second, non-consecutive term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> Additionally, both <a href="/wiki/Hamilton-Wentworth_District_School_Board" title="Hamilton-Wentworth District School Board">Public</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamilton-Wentworth_Catholic_District_School_Board" title="Hamilton-Wentworth Catholic District School Board">Catholic</a> school board trustees are elected for defined areas ranging from two trustees for multiple wards to a single trustee for an individual ward.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_city_hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hamilton_city_hall.jpg/220px-Hamilton_city_hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hamilton_city_hall.jpg/330px-Hamilton_city_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hamilton_city_hall.jpg/440px-Hamilton_city_hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamilton_city_hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Hamilton_City_Hall" title="Hamilton City Hall">Hamilton City Hall</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Hamilton,_Ontario_municipal_elections" title="List of Hamilton, Ontario municipal elections">Municipal elections</a> in Hamilton occur every four years, the last one occurring on <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario_municipal_election,_2014" title="Hamilton, Ontario municipal election, 2014">October 27, 2014</a>. The next scheduled municipal election will occur in October 2018.</p>\n<p>The Hamilton City Council is granted authority to govern by the province through the Municipal Act of Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup> As with all municipalities, the Province of Ontario has supervisory privilege over the municipality and the power to redefine, restrict or expand the powers of all municipalities in Ontario.</p>\n<p>The Criminal Code of Canada is the chief piece of legislation defining criminal conduct and penalty. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamilton_Police_Service_(Ontario)" title="Hamilton Police Service (Ontario)">Hamilton Police Service</a> is chiefly responsible for the enforcement of federal and provincial law. Although the Hamilton Police Service has authority to enforce, bylaws passed by the Hamilton City Council are mainly enforced by Provincial Offences Officers employed by the City of Hamilton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Armed_Forces" title="Canadian Armed Forces">Canadian Military</a> maintains a presence in Hamilton, with the <a href="/wiki/John_Weir_Foote" title="John Weir Foote">John Weir Foote Armoury</a> located in the downtown core on James Street North, housing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Hamilton_Light_Infantry" title="Royal Hamilton Light Infantry">Royal Hamilton Light Infantry</a> as well as the 11th Field Hamilton-Wentworth Battery and the Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders of Canada. The Hamilton Reserve Barracks, located on Pier Nine, houses the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces_Primary_Reserve" title="Canadian Forces Primary Reserve">naval reserve</a> division <a href="/wiki/HMCS_Star" title="HMCS Star">HMCS\xc2\xa0<i>Star</i></a>, 23 Service Battalion and the 23 Field Ambulance.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Hamilton is home to several post-secondary institutions that have created numerous direct and indirect jobs in education and research. <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a> moved to the city in 1930 and today has around 30,000 enrolled students, of whom almost two-thirds come from outside the immediate Hamilton region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mac_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mac-81">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MACU_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-MACU-82">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brock_University" title="Brock University">Brock University</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Catharines,_Ontario" title="St. Catharines, Ontario">St. Catharines, Ontario</a> has a satellite campus used primarily for teacher education located in Hamilton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BROCK_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-BROCK-83">[79]</a></sup> Colleges in Hamilton include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/McMaster_Divinity_College" title="McMaster Divinity College">McMaster Divinity College</a>, a Christian <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a> affiliated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist_Convention_of_Ontario_and_Quebec" title="Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec">Baptist Convention of Ontario and Quebec</a> since 1957. McMaster Divinity College is located on the McMaster University campus, and is affiliated with the university. The Divinity College was created as part of the process of passing governance of the university as a whole from the BCOQ to a privately chartered, publicly funded arrangement.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mohawk_College" title="Mohawk College">Mohawk College</a>, a college of applied arts and technology since 1967 with 10,000 full time, 40,000 part time, and 3,000 apprentice students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOHAWK_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-MOHAWK-84">[80]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Mohawk College also has an <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=IELTS_Testing_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="IELTS Testing Centre (page does not exist)">IELTS Testing Centre</a> in Hamilton at their Fennell Campus, which tests twice monthly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IELTS_Testing_Centre_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-IELTS_Testing_Centre-85">[81]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Columbia_International_College" title="Columbia International College">Columbia International College</a> is Canada\'s largest private boarding high school, with 1,700 students from 73 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Columbia_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia-86">[82]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Redeemer_University_College" title="Redeemer University College">Redeemer University College</a>, a private Christian liberal arts and science university opened in 1982, with about a thousand students currently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redeemer_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Redeemer-87">[83]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McMasterUMedical.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/220px-McMasterUMedical.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/330px-McMasterUMedical.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/McMasterUMedical.jpg/440px-McMasterUMedical.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McMasterUMedical.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMcMaster University Medical Centre</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Public education for students from kindergarten through high school is administered by three school boards. The <a href="/wiki/Hamilton-Wentworth_District_School_Board" title="Hamilton-Wentworth District School Board">Hamilton-Wentworth District School Board</a> manages 114 public schools,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton-Wentworth_Catholic_District_School_Board" title="Hamilton-Wentworth Catholic District School Board">Hamilton-Wentworth Catholic District School Board</a> operates 55 schools in the greater Hamilton area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Conseil_scolaire_Viamonde" title="Conseil scolaire Viamonde">Conseil scolaire Viamonde</a> operates one elementary and one secondary school (<a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_secondaire_Georges-P.-Vanier" title="\xc3\x89cole secondaire Georges-P.-Vanier">\xc3\x89cole secondaire Georges-P.-Vanier</a>), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conseil_scolaire_de_district_catholique_Centre-Sud" title="Conseil scolaire de district catholique Centre-Sud">Conseil scolaire de district catholique Centre-Sud</a> operates two elementary schools and one secondary school. Calvin Christian School, Providence Christian School and Timothy Christian School are independent Christian elementary schools. <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_District_Christian_High_School" title="Hamilton District Christian High School">Hamilton District Christian High School</a>, Rehoboth Christian High School and <a href="/wiki/Guido_de_Bres_Christian_High_School" title="Guido de Bres Christian High School">Guido de Bres Christian High School</a> are independent Christian high schools in the area. Both HDCH and Guido de Br\xc3\xa8s participate in the city\'s interscholastic athletics. <a href="/wiki/Hillfield_Strathallan_College" title="Hillfield Strathallan College">Hillfield Strathallan College</a> is located on the West Hamilton mountain and is a <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Accredited_Independent_Schools" title="Canadian Accredited Independent Schools">CAIS</a> member, non-profit school for children from early Montessori ages through grade twelve.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg/220px-McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg/330px-McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg/440px-McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McMaster_University_Student_Centre_Plaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMcMaster University Student Centre Plaza</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Dundas Valley School of Art is an independent art school which has serviced the Hamilton region since 1964. Students range in age from 4 years old to senior citizens and enrollment as of February 2007 was close to 4,000. In 1998, a new full-time diploma programme was launched as a joint venture with McMaster University. The faculty and staff are highly regarded regional artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvalley_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-dvalley-90">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Hamilton Conservatory for the Arts is home to many of the area\'s talented young actors, dancers, musicians, singers and visual artists. The school is equipped with a keyboard studio, spacious dance studios, art and sculpting studios, gallery space and a 300 seat recital hall. HCA offers over 90 programs for ages 3\xe2\x80\x9393, creating a "united nations" of arts under one roof.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamcon_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamcon-91">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_Literacy_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hamilton Literacy Council (page does not exist)">Hamilton Literacy Council</a> is a non-profit organization that provides basic (grades 1\xe2\x80\x935 equivalent) training in reading, writing, and math to English-speaking adults. The council\'s service is free, private, and one-to-one. It started to assist adults with their literacy skills in 1973.</p>\n<p>Hamilton is home to two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Think_tanks" title="Think tanks">think tanks</a>, the Centre for Cultural Renewal and Cardus, which deals with social architecture, culture, urbanology, economics and education and also publishes the <i>LexView Policy Journal</i> and <i>Comment Magazine</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Culture of Hamilton, Ontario">Culture of Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Media in Hamilton, Ontario">Media in Hamilton, Ontario</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People_from_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="People from Hamilton, Ontario">People from Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DundurnCastleSummer.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/DundurnCastleSummer.JPG/220px-DundurnCastleSummer.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/DundurnCastleSummer.JPG/330px-DundurnCastleSummer.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/DundurnCastleSummer.JPG/440px-DundurnCastleSummer.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DundurnCastleSummer.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Dundurn_Castle" title="Dundurn Castle">Dundurn Castle</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg/220px-Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg/330px-Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg/440px-Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gore_Park_Fountain_-_Hamilton.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGore Park Fountain. The Commerce 1 building is in the background.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hamilton has built on its historical and social background with attractions including the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Warplane_Heritage_Museum" title="Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum">Canadian Warplane Heritage Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/HMCS_Haida" title="HMCS Haida">HMCS\xc2\xa0<i>Haida</i></a> National Historic Site (Canada\'s most famous warship and the last remaining Tribal Class in the world),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HMCS_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-HMCS-93">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dundurn_Castle" title="Dundurn Castle">Dundurn Castle</a> (the residence of a Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dundurn_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-dundurn-94">[90]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens,_Ontario" title="Royal Botanical Gardens, Ontario">Royal Botanical Gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Football Hall of Fame">Canadian Football Hall of Fame</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Lion_Safari" title="African Lion Safari">African Lion Safari</a> Park, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christ_the_King_Cathedral_(Hamilton)" title="Christ the King Cathedral (Hamilton)">Cathedral of Christ the King</a>, and the Workers\' Arts and Heritage Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Founded in 1914, the <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery_of_Hamilton" title="Art Gallery of Hamilton">Art Gallery of Hamilton</a> is Ontario\'s third largest public art gallery. The gallery has over 9,000 works in its permanent collection that focus on three areas: 19th century European, Historical Canadian and Contemporary Canadian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARTGALLERY_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARTGALLERY-96">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg/220px-Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg/330px-Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg/440px-Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_James_Street_South_commercial_buildings.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHistoric James Street South commercial art buildings</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/McMaster_Museum_of_Art" title="McMaster Museum of Art">McMaster Museum of Art</a> (MMA), founded at McMaster University in 1967, houses and exhibits the university\'s art collection of more than 7,000 objects,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbook_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-fbook-97">[93]</a></sup> including historical, modern and contemporary art, the Levy Collection of Impressionist and Post-Impressionist paintings, and a collection of over 300 German Expressionist prints.</p>\n<p>Hamilton has quite an active theatre scene, with the professional company Theatre Aquarius, plus long-time amateur companies, the Players\' Guild of Hamilton and <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Theatre_Inc." title="Hamilton Theatre Inc.">Hamilton Theatre Inc.</a>. Many smaller theatre companies have also opened in the past decade, bringing a variety of theatre to the area.</p>\n<p>Growth in the arts and culture sector has garnered high-level media attention for Hamilton. A <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globe_and_Mail" title="Globe and Mail">Globe and Mail</a></i> article in 2006, entitled "Go West, Young Artist," focused on the growing art scene in Hamilton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GOWEST_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-GOWEST-16">[15]</a></sup> The Factory: Hamilton Media Arts Centre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTORY_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FACTORY-98">[94]</a></sup> opened up a new home on James Street North in 2006. Art galleries are springing up on many streets across the city: <a href="/wiki/James_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="James Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">James Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_William_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="King William Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">King William Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Locke_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="Locke Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">Locke Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="King Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">King Street</a>, to name a few. This, coupled with growth in the downtown condo market which is drawing people back to the core, is affecting the cultural fabric of the city. The opening of the Downtown Arts Centre<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAC_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-DAC-99">[95]</a></sup> on Rebecca Street has spurred further creative activities in the core. The Community Centre for Media Arts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCMA_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-CCMA-100">[96]</a></sup> (CCMA) continues to operate in downtown Hamilton. The CCMA works with marginalized populations and combines new media services such as website development, graphic design, video, and information technology, with arts education and skills development programming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INVESTH20_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-INVESTH20-101">[97]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The 2009 film <i><a href="/wiki/Defendor" title="Defendor">Defendor</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Woody_Harrelson" title="Woody Harrelson">Woody Harrelson</a> as a vigilante superhero, is implied to take place in Hamilton, referred to by its nickname of "Hammer Town" several times throughout the film. It was filmed in Hamilton and Toronto.</p>\n<p>In March 2015, Hamilton was host to the <a href="/wiki/Juno_Awards_of_2015" title="Juno Awards of 2015">JUNO Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup> which featured performances by <a href="/wiki/Hedley_(band)" title="Hedley (band)">Hedley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magic!" title="Magic!">Magic!</a>. The award ceremony was held at the FirstOntario Centre in downtown Hamilton. During JUNOfest, hundreds of local acts performed across the city, bringing thousands of tourists.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Sports in Hamilton, Ontario">Sports in Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sports_venues_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of sports venues in Hamilton, Ontario">List of sports venues in Hamilton, Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Sport_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Category:Sport in Hamilton, Ontario">Category:Sport in Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tim_Hortons_Field_Exterior.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" Centre</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_touchdown_cfhof.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" Hall of Fame</a> museum</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Professional and Semi-Professional teams</b></caption>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:left;">Club</th>\n<th Hurricanes (page does not exist)">Hamilton Hurricanes</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Junior_Football_League" title="Canadian Junior Football League">Canadian Junior Football League</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons_Field" title="Tim Hortons Field">Tim Hortons Field</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1963</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">3</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Croatia" title="Hamilton Croatia">Hamilton Croatia</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Soccer_League" title="Canadian Soccer League">Canadian Soccer League</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Brian_Timmis_Stadium" title="Brian Timmis Stadium">Brian Timmis Stadium</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1957</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamilton_Red_Wings_Jr._A" title="Hamilton Red Wings Jr. A">Hamilton Red Wings</a></td>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario_Provincial_Junior_A_Hockey_League" title="Ontario Provincial Junior A Hockey League">Ontario Provincial Junior A Hockey</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dave_Andreychuk_Mountain_Arena_%26_Skating_Centre" title="Dave Andreychuk Mountain Arena &amp; Skating Centre">Dave Andreychuk Mountain Arena</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1973</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton_Hornets_R.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hamilton Hornets R.F.C. (page does not exist)">Hamilton Hornets R.F.C.</a></td>\n<td>Niagara Rugby Union</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mohawk_Sports_Park" title="Mohawk Sports Park">Mohawk Sports Park</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1954</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Wildcats" title="Hamilton Wildcats">Hamilton Wildcats</a></td>\n<td>Australian Rules Football League</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mohawk_Sports_Park" title="Mohawk Sports Park">Mohawk Sports Park</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1997</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Cardinals" title="Hamilton Cardinals">Hamilton Cardinals</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Intercounty_Baseball_League" title="Intercounty Baseball League">Intercounty Baseball League</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Bernie_Arbour_Memorial_Stadium" title="Bernie Arbour Memorial Stadium">Bernie Arbour Memorial Stadium</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2005</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stoney_Creek_Camels&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stoney Creek Camels (page does not exist)">Stoney Creek Camels</a></td>\n<td><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rugby Ontario (page does not exist)">Marshall Rugby Premiership</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Saltfleet_District_High_School" title="Saltfleet District High School">Saltfleet District High School</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1964</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Hamilton was the host of Canada\'s first major international athletic event, the first <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> (then called the British Empire Games) in <a href="/wiki/1930_British_Empire_Games" title="1930 British Empire Games">1930</a>. Hamilton bid unsuccessfully for the Commonwealth Games in <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010</a>, losing out to <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">New Delhi</a> in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj56_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-memproj56-104">[100]</a></sup> On November 7, 2009, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalajara,_Mexico" title="Guadalajara, Mexico">Guadalajara, Mexico</a> it was announced that Toronto would host the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_Pan_Am_Games" title="2015 Pan Am Games">2015 Pan Am Games</a> after beating out two rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_American" title="South American">South American</a> cities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lima,_Peru" title="Lima, Peru">Lima, Peru</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogota,_Colombia" title="Bogota, Colombia">Bogota, Colombia</a>. The city of Hamilton co-hosted the Games with Toronto. Hamilton Mayor <a href="/wiki/Fred_Eisenberger" title="Fred Eisenberger">Fred Eisenberger</a> said, "the Pan Am Games will provide a \'unique opportunity for Hamilton to renew major sport facilities giving Hamiltonians a multi-purpose stadium, a 50-metre swimming pool, and an international-calibre <a href="/wiki/Velodrome" title="Velodrome">velodrome</a> to enjoy for generations to come.\'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PANAM_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-PANAM-105">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Around_the_Bay_Road_Race" title="Around the Bay Road Race">Around the Bay Road Race</a> circumnavigates <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour" title="Hamilton Harbour">Hamilton Harbour</a>. Although it is not a marathon distance, it is the longest continuously held long distance foot race in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj56-68_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-memproj56-68-106">[102]</a></sup> The local newspaper also hosts the amateur <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Spectator_Indoor_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Spectator Indoor Games (page does not exist)">Spectator Indoor Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj56-68_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-memproj56-68-106">[102]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hamilton has representation in two professional sports leagues, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Lacrosse" title="Major League Lacrosse">Major League Lacrosse</a>. Its major sports complexes include <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons_Field" title="Tim Hortons Field">Tim Hortons Field</a> and <a href="/wiki/FirstOntario_Centre" title="FirstOntario Centre">FirstOntario Centre</a>; Hamilton is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Football Hall of Fame">Canadian Football Hall of Fame</a> museum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foothof_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-foothof-107">[103]</a></sup> The museum hosts an annual induction event in a week-long celebration that includes school visits, a golf tournament, a formal induction dinner and concludes with the Hall of Fame game involving the local <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">CFL</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Tiger-Cats" title="Hamilton Tiger-Cats">Hamilton Tiger-Cats</a> at Tim Hortons Field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hallfame_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-hallfame-108">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IVORW_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-IVORW-109">[105]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition to team sports, Hamilton is also home to an auto race track, <a href="/wiki/Flamboro_Speedway" title="Flamboro Speedway">Flamboro Speedway</a> and Canada\'s fastest half-mile harness horse racing track, <a href="/wiki/Flamboro_Downs" title="Flamboro Downs">Flamboro Downs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flamboro_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-flamboro-110">[106]</a></sup> Another auto race track, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cayuga_International_Speedway" title="Cayuga International Speedway">Cayuga International Speedway</a>, is located near Hamilton in the <a href="/wiki/Haldimand_County" title="Haldimand County">Haldimand County</a> community of Nelles Corners, situated between <a href="/wiki/Hagersville,_Ontario" title="Hagersville, Ontario">Hagersville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cayuga,_Ontario" title="Cayuga, Ontario">Cayuga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cayuga_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cayuga-111">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hamilton hosted an NHL team in the 1920s called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamilton_Tigers_(ice_hockey)" title="Hamilton Tigers (ice hockey)">Hamilton Tigers</a>. The team folded after a players\' strike in 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TIGERSNHL1_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-TIGERSNHL1-112">[108]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_in_Motion" title="Research in Motion">Research in Motion</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jim_Balsillie" title="Jim Balsillie">Jim Balsillie</a> has shown interest in bringing another NHL team to southern Ontario. The NHL\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenix_Coyotes" title="Phoenix Coyotes">Phoenix Coyotes</a> filed for bankruptcy in 2009 and have included within their Chapter 11 reorganization a plan to sell the team to Balsillie and move the team and its operations to Hamilton, Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coyotes_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coyotes-113">[109]</a></sup> In late September, however, the bankruptcy judge did not rule in favor of Balsillie. The city plans to continue their fight for an NHL team.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of people from Hamilton, Ontario">List of people from Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Attractions">Attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_attractions_in_Hamilton,_Ontario" title="List of attractions in Hamilton, Ontario">List of attractions in Hamilton, Ontario</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamilton,_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Hamilton is a <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">sister city</a> with <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>, and its young amateur athletes compete in the <a href="/wiki/CANUSA_Games" title="CANUSA Games">CANUSA Games</a>, held alternatively in the two cities since 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memproj56_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-memproj56-104">[100]</a></sup> Flint and Hamilton hold the distinction of having the oldest continuous sister-city relationship between a U.S. and Canadian city, since 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLINTMICH_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLINTMICH-114">[110]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Other sister cities with Hamilton
